Maybe a little too helpful... they do try to tack on or suggest as many additional items to increase your total cost. < Text>
I AM SO RELIEVED TO HAVE FOUND THIS VET!

I have a long haired german shepherd who unfortunately has aggression issues with strangers. My family struggled to find a vet that we not only like, but one that created a peaceful environment for our dog, Gigi. We were always so hesitant whenever it came to vet appointments because it was always an anxious experience for all of us. < Text>
Wow. I randomly found this place and I'm glad I did!!! If you're fond of sour beers, then you have found your heaven. I got a flight of four different types of sour beer and each one was completely different from the next.  The staff was friendly and explained what a sour beer is made from and how they make their beers.

It's located in an industrial setting, so it can be hard to find. Google Maps will put you right there, though.

They have barrels aging their beer, kind of like a rick house, and it's a fun place to relax.

Go try one for yourself.<//Text>

< review>
Remember when you first tried Lambic and thought, wow, this stuff is amazing? Well, you can get sour ales‚Äîfor that is what Lambic is‚Äîclose by. Eric and the genius brewers behind their Casa Agria (Spanish for "house sour") in Oxnard have crafted a most amazing assortment of sour ales to delight and tantalize your palate (for the record, the ales I tried have not been sweet). Try the salty one (La Llorona)‚Äîdon't worry‚Äîit's only mildly salty. Or Mega Citronic‚Äîhoppy, citrusy, complex. Listening to Eric talk about his brews is like listening to a composer talk about his symphony: ‚ÄúWe collected the wild yeast in an organic field and then . . . we aged it for four months in a bourbon cask, then switched it to a port cask and finished it off with . . . " I don't remember the details, but I was spellbound listening‚Äîthese guys are off-the-chain serious about extreme creativity when it comes to brewmanship, changing and responding to what‚Äôs in season and imagineering exotic new tastes. But mostly, it's the ale. It's always about the ale. Just sip and think and enjoy. Casa Agria will be YUUGE someday, you can feel it. Now it's tiny, so go quickly and try‚Äîwhile you can still talk to Nick and company and get a dose of sour-mania first-hand.</review>

<Review>I love this place! The last 2 springs/summers we've taken our kiddo out there to pick strawberries. It's fun and educational for them to choose their favorite strawberry varieties (they have 4) while also learning about where their fresh fruits and veggies come from. It can be a little pricey for a large family but children 5 and under are free so that should alleviate some of the cost. $5 per person and $5 per pound of strawberries picked (the bags once full, are about 2 pounds each). It's nice once in a while, to get out in the sunshine and fresh air and pick some delicious fresh produce straight from the earth.<//Review><pictures>[{'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipM0rvHPSlTziqsJQnaeE0Hm2Cxk570GnsPN-G8J=w150-h150-k-no-p']}]</pictures>< Response>

< review>
This place is great for dim sum! But be prepared to wait they get really busy for dim sum if you go in the morning. They serve dim sum every day week days are cheaper than weekends though. If you go on weekends it gets super packed and crowded. If you go make sure you leave one member of your party there to hear them call your number. If you aren‚Äôt there they will skip you and give your table to someone else. The dim sum is really good for the price. There are several varieties available the sui mai is great along with several other dishes. This place is also pretty good for dinner. They have large servings that are really filling.<//review>

< review>
Don't let the name of this restaurant fool you.  If I could give a negative score...it would be a -5! We were celebrating my sis-in-laws birthday by having a family lunch. My family arrived at the end of dim sum. We were hungry so we ordered several items from the carts. My mom was very explicit that we were having lunch and wanted to get a menu so we could order the main dishes.

We sat for 1 hour, waving at the waiters and managers only to be ignored.  My mom asked for a dinner menu twice with no results.

We asked for Jasmine tea and got chrysanthemum tea. The waiter argued and said it was Jasmine.  (He's speaking to a Chinese family that owned their owned restaurant so we know what tea is being served).

Finally I got fed up and went to one of the managers and said give us our bill for the dim sum because apparently they don't serve food.  I said this in Cantonese so she knew I wasn't just some clueless Chinese American. She quickly came to our table and said she would take our order and get food served to us right away.

Food came quickly but the service sucked completely. Not one person came to wait on us. We had to get our own forks for thw kids, take out boxes and bags to pack our leftovers. As good citizens who live in America, we did the right thing and tioped 15%. But damn, I wanted to put $1 and say we are never coming back!< /review>

< Review>
This restaurant is the epitome of chaos.

There's no one to seat you. You have to flag a waiter down to seat you who will pass you off to another waiter who is confused where to seat you, and repeat this process about 5 times before they found us the most horrible spot right by the entry of the kitchen. Despite the fact that the restaurant was almost completely empty. I can't fathom why this was so hard for them and why they sat us there.

There is also no one to take your order. We had to flag someone down, fine I can deal with that. The actual ordering process was very difficult. My friend was fortunately Chinese but that apparently didn't help much. After our order was taken they still got it wrong.

One of the dishes they brought out was our 1lbs order of fresh shrimp. As my friend and I were about to eat it the waiter takes the dish away and with a very confused face and starts to just walk around with it. Back into the kitchen, back out to the dinning area, walks by us several times before bringing the dish back to us about 5 minutes later. Whaaaa just happened???? And our fresh shrimp was no longer longer hot.  I asked him where he was going with our shrimp and he ignored me.

The main thing we came here was for the fresh crab. We ordered the fried crab.  They got that wrong. Apparently on the receipt they just put down "crab" so they brought out a stir fry ginger crab. When we told them that's not what we ordered, they brought the crab back, washed off the sauce on the crab instead of getting us a fresh one and just deep fried it. The crab was SO over cooked. The meat was burnt to the shell and nearly impossible to get off. I know they did this because there was still globs of deep fried sauce stuck on the shell. The crab was extremely greasy.

They brought us 1 bowl of OLD RICE. The rice had a hard shell on the outside of it and was cold in the middle.

On top of that, the weight of the crab they put on the receipt was 2.5lbs. I fortunately cook enough dungeness crab to know that a 2.5lbs dungeness crab is HUGE. The crab they brought us was much smaller, no bigger than 1.10lbs. They overcharged us double! Beware, that kind of dishonestly I would never recommend anyone to come here.

Getting the check was a mission. I prefer not to marathon around a giant restaurant in order to get service.

Just, don't eat here. Safe yourself.< /Review>

<review>This place always gets super busy. A little advice. For dim sum, arrive around 8 or 9am just to avoid the lines. The food selection is crazy and there is so much to choose. Unless you really don't care about a big wide selection of dim sum dishes and would rather sleep in. Come around 1:30 or 2pm when it dies down. Most of the dim sum dishes are repeats. They don't cook anything new. Sadly, the truth. When you com here for dinner, make sure to come at 5pm. It doesn't get busy for dinner until 6pm. From 6pm-9pm is the dinner rush and it's a long time to wait for tables. This restaurant is huge. Thus, what needs improvement is bathrooms. They should've had a bathroom on both sides of the restaurant. It would make it more convenient. It's a great place to eat for dim sum and dinner. I have had no quarrels yet. I have been coming here since it first opened. Key thing to remember: if you come here to eat even once a month, try to familiarize yourself with staff, ask them for their names, mingle with them. This is a key strategy even if your not Chinese. I have seen my german friend jake, and he knows two of the guys in black suits.. so he can always get a seat earlier or request a dish at dim sum if he can't get it. The dinner is what attracts a bunch of people, if you order 3-4 dishes, you get a 5th dish free. but its on the posters. it's not presentable for those who don't speak chinese.
